Makeover for 10th Anniversary</span></span></nav></div></section></div><div data-at-selector-plugin-index="2" data-at-selector-plugin-name="@kl.content.Repository.ArticleBody" data-at-selector-content-key="press-releases"><article class="sc-8552822f-0 bUODRi ThemeContainer_themed__axRn3"><div class="ArticleBody_container__9sIF9"><h1 class="Header_title__OzzK0 Header_title__LzwXZ">NetTraveler Gets a Makeover for 10th Anniversary</h1><div class="ArticleBody_date__rpGhG">August 27, 2014</div><div class="ArticleBody_articleContainer__Sz0LX"><div class="ArticleBody_articleBody__gN8bN"><div class="ArticleBody_summary__K_80M ArticleBody_withContentAbove__RyYxL"><p><strong>Kaspersky Lab has observed a rise in attacks with an updated version of the “red star” APT backdoor</strong></p></div><div class="ArticleBody_content__tiVdv ArticleBody_withContentAbove__RyYxL"><p xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml"><strong>Kaspersky Lab has observed a rise in attacks with an updated version of the “red star” APT backdoor</strong>.</p><p xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml">In 2014 the actors behind global cyberespionage campaign “Operation NetTraveler” celebrate ten years of activity. Although the earliest samples appeared to have been compiled in 2005, certain indicators point to 2004 as the year when the malicious activity started. For 10 years, NetTraveler has targeted more than 350 high-profile victims in 40 countries. This year Kaspersky Lab observed an uptick in the number of attacks against Uyghur and Tibetan supporters using an updated version of the NetTraveler backdoor with a new encryption scheme. During the investigation, Kaspersky Lab discovered seven C&amp;C servers located in Hong Kong and one – in the USA.</p><h4 xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml">Recent NetTraveler victims by industries</h4><p xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml">Most recently, the main focus of interest for cyber-espionage activities revolved around diplomatic (32%), government (19%), private (11%), military (9%), industrial and infrastructure (7%), airspace (6%), research (4%), activism (3%), financial (3%), IT (3%), health (2%) and press (1%).</p><p xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml"> </p><h4 xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml">Infection method: a “newer” backdoor</h4><p xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml">Traditionally for this malicious group, the attacks started with spear-phishing e-mails targeted activists. The e-mail had two attachments, a non-malicious JPG file and a Microsoft Word .DOC file appeared to be a container with an exploit for the CVE-2012-0158 vulnerability for Microsoft Office. Kaspersky Lab determined that this malicious web archive file has been created on a system using Microsoft Office - Simplified Chinese.</p><p xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml">If run on a vulnerable version of Microsoft Office, the exploit drops the main module – Trojan-Spy. The malware configuration file has a slightly new format compared to “older” NetTraveler samples. Obviously, the developers behind NetTraveler have taken steps to try to hide the malware’s configuration.</p><p xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml">After the successful injection, NetTraveler exfiltrates common file types such as DOC, XLS, PPT, RTF and PDF.</p><h4 xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml">The discovered C&amp;C servers</h4><p xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml">Kaspersky Lab identified several command-and-control (C&amp;C) servers. Seven out of eight malicious C&amp;C servers were registered by Shanghai Meicheng Technology, and the IPs are located in Hong Kong (Trillion Company, Hongkong Dingfengxinhui Bgp Datacenter, Sun Network Limited and Hung Tai International Holdings), while the one was registered by Todaynic.com Inc with IP located in the USA (Integen Inc). Kaspersky Lab’s experts recommend blocking <a href="http://securelist.com/blog/research/66272/nettraveler-apt-gets-a-makeover-for-10th-birthday/">all malicious hosts</a> in the firewall.</p><p xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml"><em>“While investigating the NetTraveler attacks, we calculated the amount of stolen data stored on NetTraveler’s C&amp;C servers to be more than 22 gigabytes. This is an ongoing cyber-espionage campaign and, according to the last attacks against the activists, it will probably stay this way perhaps for another ten years. The most sophisticated threats appeared on surgical table of IT security companies not that long ago, but NetTraveler example shows that a disease could persist out of radar for long time”. - says Kurt Baumgartner, Principal Security Researcher at Kaspersky Lab</em>.</p><h4 xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml">Recommendations on how to stay safe from updated NetTraveler malware</h4><ul xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml"><li>Block <a href="http://securelist.com/blog/research/66272/nettraveler-apt-gets-a-makeover-for-10th-birthday/">the mentioned hosts</a> in your firewall</li><li>Update Microsoft Windows and Microsoft Office to the latest versions.</li><li>Be wary of clicking on links and opening attachments from unknown persons.</li><li>Use a secure browser such as Google Chrome, which has a faster development and patching cycle than Microsoft's Internet Explorer.</li></ul><p xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml"><em>Kaspersky Lab’s products detect and neutralize the malicious programs and its variants used by the NetTraveler Toolkit, including <strong>Trojan-Dropper.Win32.Agent.lifr</strong>,</em> Trojan-Spy.Win32.TravNet, <em><strong>Trojan-Spy.Win32.TravNet.qfr, Trojan.BAT.Tiny.b</strong> and</em> Downloader.Win32.NetTraveler.</p><p xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml"><em>Kaspersky Lab’s products detect the Microsoft Office exploits used in the spear-phishing attacks, including</em> Exploit.MSWord.CVE-2010-333, Exploit.Win32.CVE-2012-0158, <em><strong>Exploit.MSWord.CVE-2012-0158.db</strong>.</em>.</p><p xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml">To learn more about the NetTraveler operation, please read the blog post available at <a href="http://securelist.com/blog/research/66272/nettraveler-apt-gets-a-makeover-for-10th-birthday/">Securelist.com</a>.</p><p xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml"><a href="http://cybermap.kaspersky.com/">Cyberthreat real-time map</a></p><h4 xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml">Additional reading</h4><ul xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml"><li><a href="http://securelist.com/blog/research/66272/nettraveler-apt-gets-a-makeover-for-10th-birthday/">NetTraveler APT Gets A Makeover For 10th Birthday</a></li><li><a href="http://securelist.com/blog/research/35936/nettraveler-is-running-red-star-apt-attacks-compromise-high-profile-victims/">"NetTraveler is Running!" - Red Star APT Attacks Compromise High-Profile Victims</a></li><li><a href="http://securelist.com/blog/incidents/57455/nettraveler-is-back-the-red-star-apt-returns-with-new-tricks/">NetTraveler Is Back: The 'Red Star' APT Returns With New Tricks</a></li></ul><br xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml" /></div></div></div></div></article><div class="ArticleSearchEngine_onlyForSearchEngine__m_HB2" itemscope="" itemType="http://schema.org/Article"><meta itemscope="" itemProp="mainEntityOfPage" itemType="https://schema.org/WebPage" With over a billion devices protected to date from emerging cyberthreats and targeted attacks, Kaspersky’s deep threat intelligence and security expertise is constantly transforming into innovative solutions and services to protect individuals, businesses, critical infrastructure, and governments around the globe. The company’s comprehensive security portfolio includes leading digital life protection for personal devices, specialized security products and services for companies, as well as Cyber Immune solutions to fight sophisticated and evolving digital threats. We help millions of individuals and nearly 200,000 corporate clients protect what matters most to them. Although the earliest samples appeared to have been compiled in 2005, certain indicators point to 2004 as the year when the malicious activity started. For 10 years, NetTraveler has targeted more than 350 high-profile victims in 40 countries. This year Kaspersky Lab observed an uptick in the number of attacks against Uyghur and Tibetan supporters using an updated version of the NetTraveler backdoor with a new encryption scheme. During the investigation, Kaspersky Lab discovered seven C\u0026amp;C servers located in Hong Kong and one – in the USA.\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch4 xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml\"\u003eRecent NetTraveler victims by industries\u003c/h4\u003e\u003cp xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml\"\u003eMost recently, the main focus of interest for cyber-espionage activities revolved around diplomatic (32%), government (19%), private (11%), military (9%), industrial and infrastructure (7%), airspace (6%), research (4%), activism (3%), financial (3%), IT (3%), health (2%) and press (1%).\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml\"\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003ch4 xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml\"\u003eInfection method: a “newer” backdoor\u003c/h4\u003e\u003cp xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml\"\u003eTraditionally for this malicious group, the attacks started with spear-phishing e-mails targeted activists. The e-mail had two attachments, a non-malicious JPG file and a Microsoft Word .DOC file appeared to be a container with an exploit for the CVE-2012-0158 vulnerability for Microsoft Office. Kaspersky Lab determined that this malicious web archive file has been created on a system using Microsoft Office - Simplified Chinese.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml\"\u003eIf run on a vulnerable version of Microsoft Office, the exploit drops the main module – Trojan-Spy. The malware configuration file has a slightly new format compared to “older” NetTraveler samples. Obviously, the developers behind NetTraveler have taken steps to try to hide the malware’s configuration.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml\"\u003eAfter the successful injection, NetTraveler exfiltrates common file types such as DOC, XLS, PPT, RTF and PDF.\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch4 xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml\"\u003eThe discovered C\u0026amp;C servers\u003c/h4\u003e\u003cp xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml\"\u003eKaspersky Lab identified several command-and-control (C\u0026amp;C) servers. Seven out of eight malicious C\u0026amp;C servers were registered by Shanghai Meicheng Technology, and the IPs are located in Hong Kong (Trillion Company, Hongkong Dingfengxinhui Bgp Datacenter, Sun Network Limited and Hung Tai International Holdings), while the one was registered by Todaynic.com Inc with IP located in the USA (Integen Inc). Kaspersky Lab’s experts recommend blocking \u003ca href=\"http://securelist.com/blog/research/66272/nettraveler-apt-gets-a-makeover-for-10th-birthday/\"\u003eall malicious hosts\u003c/a\u003e in the firewall.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml\"\u003e\u003cem\u003e“While investigating the NetTraveler attacks, we calculated the amount of stolen data stored on NetTraveler’s C\u0026amp;C servers to be more than 22 gigabytes. This is an ongoing cyber-espionage campaign and, according to the last attacks against the activists, it will probably stay this way perhaps for another ten years. The most sophisticated threats appeared on surgical table of IT security companies not that long ago, but NetTraveler example shows that a disease could persist out of radar for long time”. - says Kurt Baumgartner, Principal Security Researcher at Kaspersky Lab\u003c/em\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch4 xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml\"\u003eRecommendations on how to stay safe from updated NetTraveler malware\u003c/h4\u003e\u003cul xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml\"\u003e\u003cli\u003eBlock \u003ca href=\"http://securelist.com/blog/research/66272/nettraveler-apt-gets-a-makeover-for-10th-birthday/\"\u003ethe mentioned hosts\u003c/a\u003e in your firewall\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003eUpdate Microsoft Windows and Microsoft Office to the latest versions.\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003eBe wary of clicking on links and opening attachments from unknown persons.\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003eUse a secure browser such as Google Chrome, which has a faster development and patching cycle than Microsoft's Internet Explorer.\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003cp xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml\"\u003e\u003cem\u003eKaspersky Lab’s products detect and neutralize the malicious programs and its variants used by the NetTraveler Toolkit, including \u003cstrong\u003eTrojan-Dropper.Win32.Agent.lifr\u003c/strong\u003e,\u003c/em\u003e Trojan-Spy.Win32.TravNet, \u003cem\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eTrojan-Spy.Win32.TravNet.qfr, Trojan.BAT.Tiny.b\u003c/strong\u003e and\u003c/em\u003e Downloader.Win32.NetTraveler.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml\"\u003e\u003cem\u003eKaspersky Lab’s products detect the Microsoft Office exploits used in the spear-phishing attacks, including\u003c/em\u003e Exploit.MSWord.CVE-2010-333, Exploit.Win32.CVE-2012-0158, \u003cem\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eExploit.MSWord.CVE-2012-0158.db\u003c/strong\u003e.\u003c/em\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml\"\u003eTo learn more about the NetTraveler operation, please read the blog post available at \u003ca href=\"http://securelist.com/blog/research/66272/nettraveler-apt-gets-a-makeover-for-10th-birthday/\"\u003eSecurelist.com\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml\"\u003e\u003ca href=\"http://cybermap.kaspersky.com/\"\u003eCyberthreat real-time map\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch4 xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml\"\u003eAdditional reading\u003c/h4\u003e\u003cul xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml\"\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003ca
